  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b57924f3-257a-4c6d-a04e-eb536a2a8733'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText2553520405769417266" style="display:none">Phil Hastings was a lucky man-he had money, a growing reputation as a screenwriter, a happy, loving family with three kids, and he'd just moved into the house of his dreams in rural of magic-and about to be altered irrevocably by a magic more real than any he dared imagine. For with the Magic came the Bad Thing, and the Faerie, and then the cool. . .and the resurrection of a primordial war with a forgotten people-a war that not only the Hastings but the whole human race could lose."A contemporary novel of masterful horror replete with magic, fantasy, and more than a little stylish eroticism."-- "The Washington Post.<br /><br />" "Feist writes skillfully and his imagination is prolific."-- "Rave Reviews." "<br /><br />" "Absorbing, though-provoking, and thoroughly magical. Feist's skillfully crafted prose illuminates many of the darker sides of fairy stories. . .Try it as a bedtime story. . .but only on nights when you can take some time getting to sleep."-- "The West Coast Review Of Books ."</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/28790614?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="L" class="user" itemprop="url" name="L" href="/user/show/1156396-l">L</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1156396-l?shelf=fantasy-supernatural">fantasy-supernatural</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer28790614" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6286339608824992646">I decided that it was time to re-read this one. Even though I've read this twice already, Feist is scaring the crap out of me, to the point that I have to set it aside sometimes. I will be with it for a few more days, I'm sure, even though I'm putting today's date on the review. I can do this because I know my rating won't change, esp. since GoodReads doesn't let a person give a book more than 5 stars. Damn, this is scary!<br/><br/>Feist is certainly one of the best in the genre. His descriptions of the w</span>
  <span id="freeText6286339608824992646" style="display:none">I decided that it was time to re-read this one. Even though I've read this twice already, Feist is scaring the crap out of me, to the point that I have to set it aside sometimes. I will be with it for a few more days, I'm sure, even though I'm putting today's date on the review. I can do this because I know my rating won't change, esp. since GoodReads doesn't let a person give a book more than 5 stars. Damn, this is scary!<br /><br />Feist is certainly one of the best in the genre. His descriptions of the worlds he visits are vivid; you not only see them, you feel them. His characters are absolutely real (including the fantasy &amp; supernatural ones). This is the first of Feist's works that I read, and on re-reading, the magic holds. For my money, this is his best. Feist, like King and children themselves, knows that kids are often the targets of the Bad Things and that they must and do struggle with evil; he doesn't shy away from these truths. His magical beings live in a different, sometimes overlapping, reality, with it's own rules. The blurbs refer to the book as "harrowing" and "forboding." Both are true. This is one scary tale, on multiple levels. Enjoy! Just don't read it home alone, in the dark.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6286339608824992646" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_18291900" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18291900" />
    <a title="Dee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/618055-dee"><img alt="Dee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480108808p2/618055.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/18291900?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dee" href="/user/show/618055-dee">Dee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/618055-dee?shelf=fantasy-modern">fantasy-modern</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18291900" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17142441637988461567">The first quarter of the book was slow and a little clunky; I felt it very contrived and awkward, almost like the author wasn't quite sure how to get all his characters in one place, or how to introduce them once he brought them to the same location. That said, the remaining 3/4 of the book is excellent. Feist doesn't exactly put a new "spin" on faeries, but his descriptions of them are marvelously complex. Faeries are not merely human with pointy ears and gem-colored eyes; they are hyper-sexual</span>
  <span id="freeText17142441637988461567" style="display:none">The first quarter of the book was slow and a little clunky; I felt it very contrived and awkward, almost like the author wasn't quite sure how to get all his characters in one place, or how to introduce them once he brought them to the same location. That said, the remaining 3/4 of the book is excellent. Feist doesn't exactly put a new "spin" on faeries, but his descriptions of them are marvelously complex. Faeries are not merely human with pointy ears and gem-colored eyes; they are hyper-sexual, capricious creatures that have few features of humanity about them at all. Even the "good" faeries have a streak of weirdness and cruel humor. The plot moves along fairly well after the initial slowness, and there are some interesting twists and developments with secret societies and ancient history. Worth a read if you are interested in the "modern faerie" type stories. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17142441637988461567" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_18352195" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18352195" />
    <a title="Werner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/903390-werner"><img alt="Werner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1216337931p2/903390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/18352195?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Werner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Werner" href="/user/show/903390-werner">Werner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385236232" href="/book/show/1017161.Faerie_Tale">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of fantasy, and of supernatural fiction</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/903390-werner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18352195" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9116608952219395958">Raymond E. Feist (b. 1945) is one of the leading fantasy writers in the contemporary U.S. literary scene, best known for his massive Riftwar Saga series. Barb and I read the latter in the early 90s and liked it, although I've never reviewed it here and we never followed it up with any of the succeeding series. (I was inclined to think there was a limit to how many magical existential threats one kingdom in a fantasy world could realistically be expected to encounter in succession, and suspected </span>
  <span id="freeText9116608952219395958" style="display:none">Raymond E. Feist (b. 1945) is one of the leading fantasy writers in the contemporary U.S. literary scene, best known for his massive Riftwar Saga series. Barb and I read the latter in the early 90s and liked it, although I've never reviewed it here and we never followed it up with any of the succeeding series. (I was inclined to think there was a limit to how many magical existential threats one kingdom in a fantasy world could realistically be expected to encounter in succession, and suspected that the severe case of "sequelitis" was mostly an attempt to milk the setting/characters for more cash.) That said, I did think the first series was involving and well-written, with lifelike characters who are engaging and a plot that's often emotionally compelling; it also didn't feel so dependent on Tolkien as Terry Brooks' Shannara series opener.<br /><br />However, my first introduction to Feist's work was this stand-alone novel, read as a public library check-out a few years earlier, not long after it was published. I still consider it the best of his books that I've read, and it made a strong enough impression on my memory that I feel comfortable reviewing it, after more than 30 years, without having a copy in front of me. (Though it will necessarily be a shorter and less detailed review than some of mine are!)<br /><br />In the author's present, a well-to-do family (very successful Hollywood scriptwriter, his second wife, roughly 20-year-old daughter from his first marriage, and a pair of boys on the cusp of their teens) move into a long-empty old country house, Erl King Hill, in the wilds of upstate New York. It doesn't take long --like, about the first page!-- for the reader to be made aware that this house and its environs are a habitat for the Fae, and a place where their reality intersects with ours; and it turns out that there's even much, much more and deeper significance to the connection than that. Feist will disclose all of his mysteries only in his own good time, and meanwhile all of the Hastings family members are in for a puzzling, stressful, and ultimately scary and potentially lethal adventure.<br /><br />Interaction of the supernatural with the mundane world is a motif I really like in fiction, and it's here in spades. (A few scenes here take place in Faerie, so I've classified this as fantasy; but the bulk of the tale plays out in this world; I've recommended it for fans of supernatural fiction as well.) Much actual traditional lore about the Fae from European cultures (mostly Celtic and Germanic) is worked in here very nicely, such as the Wild Hunt, Wieland the smith, the Seelie and the Unseelie Courts; we even have a cameo appearance of Thomas the Rhymer. All of the Hastings family members are likable characters that you root for and wish well, and they all play significant roles in the story, including the boys (who get to show their mettle). The other characters are also vital and realistic. Feist does a great job with his plotting, and he provides some romance to add pleasant flavor to the stew; it has an insta-love quality, but despite that quibble (and despite some implied premarital sex) it comes across as genuine love. (This isn't a kid's book, despite the two younger characters, but there's no explicit sex and bad language is restrained --there are two f-words, but in perspective, it's a 420-page book). It's not a deep read that grapples much with profound spiritual or philosophical questions; but for me it was a really enjoyable, page-turning read. (If Goodreads used half stars in its rating system, I'd actually have given the book 4 and 1/2.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="9116608952219395958" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1437736325" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1437736325" />
    <a title="Thomas Strömquist" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32669562-thomas-str-mquist"><img alt="Thomas Strömquist" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590007844p2/32669562.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas Strömquist" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas Strömquist" href="/user/show/32669562-thomas-str-mquist">Thomas Strömquist</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/27358005-faerie-tale">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32669562-thomas-str-mquist?shelf=glad-to-have-read-it-never-again">glad-to-have-read-it-never-again</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1437736325" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12797889644467314994">Ok, first let me go ahead and say that this is a true "GoodReads-2-star-rating", that is "it was ok" and nothing else. because it is really ok - if you are into fantasy and in particular faeries and the whole "Celtic" mythology I would certainly recommend it. It's well written and well thought out.<br/><br/>My own problems, however, were threefold; first, I really don't like fantasy and it's my firm belief that this will be my last book to fit into that category. I came to believe that this one would tilt</span>
  <span id="freeText12797889644467314994" style="display:none">Ok, first let me go ahead and say that this is a true "GoodReads-2-star-rating", that is "it was ok" and nothing else. because it is really ok - if you are into fantasy and in particular faeries and the whole "Celtic" mythology I would certainly recommend it. It's well written and well thought out.<br><br>My own problems, however, were threefold; first, I really don't like fantasy and it's my firm belief that this will be my last book to fit into that category. I came to believe that this one would tilt more in the "horror"-direction and it did in parts and all should have been well with that if it wasn't for problem two; mythology and mythological creatures. Some are, when treated by a good writer, very good horror characters. Others,<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447590256i/17024832.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>not so much.<br><br>The narrative is really detailed and dense, if you are a very fast reader and/or love the subject matter, I'm sure you won't mind or be bothered, because the writing is good. If neither of those are true, you are in for a chore. The final 100 pages could have been 30 and none would have been lost. At times i thought I mistakenly started over on a page, because whole chunks of story are rehashed with very little variation. near the very end, we are treated to things such as two full pages of dialogue in between two chimes of a church bell.<br><br>Also (yes I know I said 3, but this is not a 'problem' I had, more of an annoyance) we are treated to the 'child hero', the one who has close to ruined some of Stephen King's and other great novels, not to mention a number of movies. It wasn't so bad in this book, but I never enjoy them. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12797889644467314994" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1437736325">
  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_125865161" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/125865161" />
    <a title="[Name Redacted]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/287915-name-redacted"><img alt="[Name Redacted]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347082397p2/287915.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/125865161?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="[Name Redacted]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="[Name Redacted]" href="/user/show/287915-name-redacted">[Name Redacted]</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780553277838" href="/book/show/317503.Faerie_Tale">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer125865161" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8177162442486186135">To give this book ANY stars would be giving it too many. <br/><br/>The concept is good, but the pacing is terrible (a slow, ponderous plot), there's a surplus of characters (none of them terribly engaging or real), and it takes seemingly-forever to get to the point. <br/><br/>Worst of all, this book seems to have heralded the start of what my friends and I (at the age of TWELVE) disgustedly referred to as Raymond E. Feist's "rape-fantasy period" in which he seems to relish explicitly describing the rape/abuse of hi</span>
  <span id="freeText8177162442486186135" style="display:none">To give this book ANY stars would be giving it too many. <br /><br />The concept is good, but the pacing is terrible (a slow, ponderous plot), there's a surplus of characters (none of them terribly engaging or real), and it takes seemingly-forever to get to the point. <br /><br />Worst of all, this book seems to have heralded the start of what my friends and I (at the age of TWELVE) disgustedly referred to as Raymond E. Feist's "rape-fantasy period" in which he seems to relish explicitly describing the rape/abuse of his female characters. This book appears to have been the first and was easily the worst as the female character is actually described as WANTING it to take place for a portion of the rape. That scene alone told me more than I ever wanted to know about Raymond E. Feist's psyche, and when i realized that nearly every subsequent book he wrote up until 1995 (when I stopped giving him the benefit of the doubt) ALSO included a similar scene, I gave up on him as an author and literally threw all the Feist books I owned from that period in the garbage. He may have improved after that, I don't know and I haven't bothered to find out.<br /><br />If you want a good take on a similar theme, I recommend just about anything by Charles De Lint or Holly Black -- steer clear of this one however.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8177162442486186135" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2337414116" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2337414116" />
    <a title="Eric" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36502262-eric"><img alt="Eric" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1501438390p2/36502262.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2337414116?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eric" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eric" href="/user/show/36502262-eric">Eric</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6637609-faerie-tale">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36502262-eric?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36502262-eric?shelf=raymond-e-feist">raymond-e-feist</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2337414116" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2378064445919356324">3.5 Stars<br/><br/>A solid read meshing horror with a fantasy tale about a family who discovers faerie legends are far more real than they ever imagined. <br/><br/>Despite loving the Riftwar books and all the subsequent sequels and series, I had never even heard of this book until a coworker told me about it. The setup sounds like it’s straight from a horror movie. A family moves to a rural area, settling in an older home. The family has young children and a mostly grown daughter (who is, of course, attractive). Th</span>
  <span id="freeText2378064445919356324" style="display:none">3.5 Stars<br /><br />A solid read meshing horror with a fantasy tale about a family who discovers faerie legends are far more real than they ever imagined. <br /><br />Despite loving the Riftwar books and all the subsequent sequels and series, I had never even heard of this book until a coworker told me about it. The setup sounds like it’s straight from a horror movie. A family moves to a rural area, settling in an older home. The family has young children and a mostly grown daughter (who is, of course, attractive). There are all kinds of local stories and legends about some woods nearby, including a few mysteries occurrences. <br /><br />Where the book differed from so many horror movies is the faerie element. Instead of some demented killer in the woods, there are wonderful, terrifying, fantastic creatures from legend. As the story progresses, the family comes into contact with some of these creatures, slowly realizing that there is something in the woods, even if they don’t understand it. <br /><br />This was an entertaining book, and I finished it in less than 2 days. One of the strengths was the portrayal of the various faeries. These are no simple, benign creatures. The faeries in this story are fantastic, beautiful, but utterly alien creatures. I liked how the author showed their allure as well as their danger. <br /><br />I did have a few issues, though. The pace was a bit slow as the author built tension. However, instead of continuing to build and escalate, the tension plateaued and remained steady. My other main issue is that throughout the novel I was never emotionally engaged. I never connected to the characters, which meant that I was never as caught up with the events as I’d like. <br /><br />Despite a couple small complaints, this was a solid, entertaining read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2378064445919356324" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_4368259" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/4368259" />
    <a title="LJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/250195-lj"><img alt="LJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1436467895p2/250195.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/4368259?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="LJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="LJ" href="/user/show/250195-lj">LJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=pennsylvania">pennsylvania</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=contemporary_post_1945">contemporary_post_1945</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=male_author">male_author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=paranormal_fantasy">paranormal_fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer4368259" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17736942861447845566">FAERIE TALE (Suspense/Fantasy-Hasting Family-Pennsylvania-Cont) – VG<br/>Feist, Raymond, E. –Standalone<br/>Doubleday, 1988, US Hardcover – ISBN: 9780385236232<br/>First Sentence: Barney Doyle sat at his cluttered workbench, attempting to fix Olaf Andersen’s ancient power mower for the fourth time in seven years. <br/>*** Phil Hastings, his wife Gloria, his daughter Gabbie and their twin boys Patrick and Sean move from Sunny California to an old farmhouse in upstate New York whose land includes virgin forest. They </span>
  <span id="freeText17736942861447845566" style="display:none">FAERIE TALE (Suspense/Fantasy-Hasting Family-Pennsylvania-Cont) – VG<br />Feist, Raymond, E. –Standalone<br />Doubleday, 1988, US Hardcover – ISBN: 9780385236232<br />First Sentence: Barney Doyle sat at his cluttered workbench, attempting to fix Olaf Andersen’s ancient power mower for the fourth time in seven years. <br />*** Phil Hastings, his wife Gloria, his daughter Gabbie and their twin boys Patrick and Sean move from Sunny California to an old farmhouse in upstate New York whose land includes virgin forest. They soon find they have more to contend with than they expected. Unexpected, and unexplainable, encounters with strange creatures, the boy’s acknowledgement of “the Bad Thing” living under a bridge and Gabbie’s almost sexual encounter with a farrier who died over a hundred years ago are only some of the strange goings on which threaten the family.<br />*** I love this book and read it every year or so on Midsummer’s Day (June 24th). However, this is not your child’s faerie tale even though it involves brotherly love and courage. It is fantasy; it is horror. It is creepy, dark, at times violent, at times sexual and always a page-turner. Those who love Celtic myth and Shakespeare will recognize magical elements of The Fool, elf-shot, Trooping Faeires, and more. It is one of those rare books that makes you feel as though it “could” be possible and causes even non-Catholics to wish for a vial of holy water, a silver sword and a true faerie stone.. Each time I read it, I find myself researching the legends and faerie folk involved, looking for erl-king hills and avoiding faeire rings at midnight on Midsummer’s Night and All-Hallow’s Eve. Next year, I’ll remember to start earlier in the day so I’m not up until midnight finishing it. At least I wasn’t in the woods. It’s the blending of fantasy in contemporary life which, to me, makes this book so compelling, frightening and memorable. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17736942861447845566" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_961176980" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/961176980" />
    <a title="Nathan Johnson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978492-nathan-johnson"><img alt="Nathan Johnson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408813644p2/3978492.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/961176980?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nathan Johnson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nathan Johnson" href="/user/show/3978492-nathan-johnson">Nathan Johnson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer961176980" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13348153661712325808">Parts of this book were quite good. It had the makings of a fine story.<br/><br/>However, it was ruined by a few things.<br/><br/><br/>1) Too many Mary-Sue characters. The father is an uber successful author/screenwriter that can afford anything. His wife is a semi-famous actress that could retire early due to husband's wealth. The daughter has a trust fund in the millions, and her boyfriend is somehow also a great screenwriter in the making. Everything about these characters is just too perfect, they have everything go</span>
  <span id="freeText13348153661712325808" style="display:none">Parts of this book were quite good. It had the makings of a fine story.<br /><br />However, it was ruined by a few things.<br /><br /><br />1) Too many Mary-Sue characters. The father is an uber successful author/screenwriter that can afford anything. His wife is a semi-famous actress that could retire early due to husband's wealth. The daughter has a trust fund in the millions, and her boyfriend is somehow also a great screenwriter in the making. Everything about these characters is just too perfect, they have everything going for them.<br /><br />2) A bit of SPOILER here. I do NOT like books that contain rape. I just don't feel like many authors get it right and it disturbs me. Feist doesn't do a very good job with it either. At one point the daughter is raped by... a bad faeirie. But it was sloppily and disturbingly written. Like it was just pushed into the book for effect. I DID like how the family reacted, it was a good concern for their daughter.<br />However, they didn't seem too worried that there might be a terrible rapist running around in the woods. They only change their routine by making their two sons stay near the house. That is it. The daughter has some reaction to being raped, but it is mostly her reaction to the strange faeirie happenings in the area, and NOT about her violation.<br /><br /><br />The last part of the book just spiraled downward and ended about how you might expect.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13348153661712325808" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_241458440" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/241458440" />
    <a title="Edafe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5668214-edafe"><img alt="Edafe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592133650p2/5668214.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/241458440?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edafe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edafe" href="/user/show/5668214-edafe">Edafe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Dan Brown</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer241458440" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1272174336976552036">150 pages in and really enjoying the pacing of this story. I was a tad concerned after reading some of the comments but it's a gripping read.<br/><br/>There were several polarised opinions on this book and I ummed and ahhed for some time before making use of free ebook lending at my local library.<br/><br/>Raymond E Feist reads like an early Dan Brown, the characters are there primarily to move the action forward. The weaving of the tale is the star in this book, not individual characters. Basically, it's the equiv</span>
  <span id="freeText1272174336976552036" style="display:none">150 pages in and really enjoying the pacing of this story. I was a tad concerned after reading some of the comments but it's a gripping read.<br /><br />There were several polarised opinions on this book and I ummed and ahhed for some time before making use of free ebook lending at my local library.<br /><br />Raymond E Feist reads like an early Dan Brown, the characters are there primarily to move the action forward. The weaving of the tale is the star in this book, not individual characters. Basically, it's the equivalent of a big budget special effects film with a great plot, it's not a character study or deep drama. <br /><br />The pace is cracking, it starts of fairly sedately, introducing us to the displaced family from California settling into a rural idyll. A minor grumble: they are a little too flush with fortune for my tastes, though this is used to great effect later on and actually makes sense by the finale.<br /><br />Feist sets up some scenes to discombobulate the reader early on but it's well into the first third of the book before the plot kicks into high gear. It's probably disparaging the quality of the writing to compare him to Dan Brown but he is the first writer who popped into my mind as I became gripped in the tale.<br /><br />Some points for readers of a delicate disposition: there are scenes concerning sexual assault on pre-teens. While I can understand the disgust this brings to some readers, I do strongly believe that was the intended reaction. We are meant to be disgusted, repelled and horrified, I don't think Feist adds these scenes gratuitously, however it may be a deal breaker for some.<br /><br />4 instead of 5 stars as there were clunky scenes, some decisions made no sense at all for the characters involved. This was mostly towards the finale and I can't hold too much of a grudge against Feist for an otherwise compelling adventure.<br /><br />~A special thinks to my "secretary" for typing up my review and to my Kindle for making reading possible with my arm in a sling!~<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1272174336976552036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_306285612" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/306285612" />
    <a title="Michael Fierce" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6880123-michael-fierce"><img alt="Michael Fierce" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602282713p2/6880123.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/306285612?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Fierce" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Fierce" href="/user/show/6880123-michael-fierce">Michael Fierce</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780553277838" href="/book/show/317503.Faerie_Tale">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">lovers of urban fantasy, dark fantasy, fans of Stephen King</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6880123-michael-fierce?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6880123-michael-fierce?shelf=favorite-books">favorite-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6880123-michael-fierce?shelf=dark-fantasy">dark-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer306285612" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4323629677755247264">I bought this book because I was a big fan of Raymond E. Feist's "Riftwar Saga", and was I ever super-glad I did! This book is better! This is urban fantasy that Charles De Lint would later make a full career out of. Only, it isn't really anything like Charle De Lint. It would be more accurate to describe this as an urban fantasy as if written by Stephen King at the top of his form. Not to say that the book doesn't have a few flaws that I've probably overlooked over the years, if it's true than </span>
  <span id="freeText4323629677755247264" style="display:none">I bought this book because I was a big fan of Raymond E. Feist's "Riftwar Saga", and was I ever super-glad I did! This book is better! This is urban fantasy that Charles De Lint would later make a full career out of. Only, it isn't really anything like Charle De Lint. It would be more accurate to describe this as an urban fantasy as if written by Stephen King at the top of his form. Not to say that the book doesn't have a few flaws that I've probably overlooked over the years, if it's true than I will just have to defend it and say that this book is flawsome! (flaws + awesome = flawsome!). It's about the Hastings, including their dog and cat, coming into contact with the world of Faerie which is practically in their back yard. Unforgettable situations. Unforgettable characters. For those of you who get mad at a lot of books because they don't have good endings, you have nothing to worry about here. I loved the ending. And I love this book which I've re-read several times and given it to my sister who loved it, who in turn let our younger sister read it, who loved it, and I also gave it to the wife of my old guitarist friend who is a fairy collector and a borderline lover / hater with everything she reads, annnnnnd..she LOVED it! So, there! If you are a book connoiseur like me, track down the 1989 Bantam Spectra 1st paperback edition with the gatefold cover art by Chris Hopkins, which is incredible. As a note, I read this back-to-back with Piers Anthony's "Shade Of The Tree" and have done so many times since. For some unknown reason, they go hand-in-hand for me. Maybe they would for you too. At the very least, they make for a great double-punch of dark fantasy / horror comparable to Stephen King. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4323629677755247264" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_17172055" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/17172055" />
    <a title="Damon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/962480-damon"><img alt="Damon" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/17172055?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Damon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Damon" href="/user/show/962480-damon">Damon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who likes fantasy fiction</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer17172055" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17547254605501698797">Raymond E Feist has built an impressive catalog, and even been likened to a modern day Tolkein. While I don't dispute that, I can say that I find Feist's work eminently more accessible, and therefor more enjoyable than a trip to Middle Earth. Typically, he sets his stories in the Realm he first began to create with "Magician: Apprentice". Faerie Tale, however, is set in a modern day home, inhabited by modern day people, in a modern day United States. But what the characters experience is anythin</span>
  <span id="freeText17547254605501698797" style="display:none">Raymond E Feist has built an impressive catalog, and even been likened to a modern day Tolkein. While I don't dispute that, I can say that I find Feist's work eminently more accessible, and therefor more enjoyable than a trip to Middle Earth. Typically, he sets his stories in the Realm he first began to create with "Magician: Apprentice". Faerie Tale, however, is set in a modern day home, inhabited by modern day people, in a modern day United States. But what the characters experience is anything but modern. Using well researched information about the "Little Folk", Feist weaves a spellbinding, and at times frightening, tale about what happens when folk lore and legends turn out to be real, and how it may be helpful to pay attention to the eccentric person down the street who can recount the fairy tales of his childhood with clarity. Feist somehow makes it all seem so plausible, that when a Troll begins to menace some children under a bridge, it can make you shiver. I won't go into detail, since the story begs to be read, but I will say that it is a gem that should not be missed. I wish a studio would option it for production.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17547254605501698797" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_38561746" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38561746" />
    <a title="Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/345449-elizabeth"><img alt="Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1407970030p2/345449.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/38561746?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth" href="/user/show/345449-elizabeth">Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38561746" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1833255616872557374">This book has been recommended to me by several people over the years. Ultimately, though, I was disappointed by it. I found the story dated and formulaic, and the ending a bit too pat and rushed.<br/><br/>Written before there was such a term as 'urban fantasy', this book would fall into that category: beings of myth interacting with the modern world. It's my favorite genre, but is much better served by authors such as Charles de Lint, Neil Gaiman, Emma Bull, and others of that ilk. <br/><br/>The author did his res</span>
  <span id="freeText1833255616872557374" style="display:none">This book has been recommended to me by several people over the years. Ultimately, though, I was disappointed by it. I found the story dated and formulaic, and the ending a bit too pat and rushed.<br /><br />Written before there was such a term as 'urban fantasy', this book would fall into that category: beings of myth interacting with the modern world. It's my favorite genre, but is much better served by authors such as Charles de Lint, Neil Gaiman, Emma Bull, and others of that ilk. <br /><br />The author did his research, but in the end I didn't much like what he did with it. I'm something of a student of Faerie, and I found that the evil character didn't ring true to the lore I have read. I also found the father character to be a bit of a Mary-Sue, and the teenage daughter character to be unrealistic. I didn't like what he did with the mother character at all; she was not very well rounded, almost an afterthought in a lot of scenes.<br /><br />I wouldn't recommend this book to anyone who really loves urban or mythic fantasy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1833255616872557374" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272081-vivienne?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272081-vivienne?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/272081-vivienne?shelf=faerie">faerie</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1303273478" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11514372208828964080">This is the only stand alone novel that Feist has written. I read it many years ago and recently acquired it for my Kindle. When adding it to Goodreads I accidentally marked it as read, which led to a comment from a friend who shares my passion for Faerie. This exchange prompted me to start reading rather than just add to my very long TBR list.<br/><br/>I had forgotten the details of the plot so this was almost like a fresh read. I felt it held up well and overall certainly was an intelligent yet quite un</span>
  <span id="freeText11514372208828964080" style="display:none">This is the only stand alone novel that Feist has written. I read it many years ago and recently acquired it for my Kindle. When adding it to Goodreads I accidentally marked it as read, which led to a comment from a friend who shares my passion for Faerie. This exchange prompted me to start reading rather than just add to my very long TBR list.<br /><br />I had forgotten the details of the plot so this was almost like a fresh read. I felt it held up well and overall certainly was an intelligent yet quite unsettling tale of the Fae. There are a few scenes worthy of <i>The Exorcist</i> in terms of disturbing horror involving children. Although set firmly in late 1980s New England, Feist draws upon various strands of faerie lore including Shakespeare, the tale of Thomas the Rhymer and Scottish and Irish folklore. <br /><br />A terrific, chilling tale. I also loved the new cover art that was very reminiscent of Alan Lee's work.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11514372208828964080" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9125139787347833600"><i>Faerie Tale</i> is one of those books, for me at least, that does not get better with age. The first time I read it, I enjoyed it. The second time, I couldn't remember why I liked it to begin with. It's the only book that I've really had that type of reaction to. I've liked books less when I've gone back and re-read them, but not that much. It was like watching the old, original <i>Battlestar Galactica</i> as a child and then re-watching it as a college student- I guess I liked the Vipers, but gosh, I didn</span>
  <span id="freeText9125139787347833600" style="display:none"><i>Faerie Tale</i> is one of those books, for me at least, that does not get better with age. The first time I read it, I enjoyed it. The second time, I couldn't remember why I liked it to begin with. It's the only book that I've really had that type of reaction to. I've liked books less when I've gone back and re-read them, but not that much. It was like watching the old, original <i>Battlestar Galactica</i> as a child and then re-watching it as a college student- I guess I liked the Vipers, but gosh, I didn't realize how sexist it was, and where did a prostitute learn to sky dive?<br /><br />My problem upon re-reading <i>Faerie Tale</i> was twofold. It isn't as "cool" as it thinks it is, and the female characters were off. </span>

  <span id="freeText1064098048547940647" style="display:none">Really a 4.5...a deliciously creepy tale of what happens when the Hastings family bump up against the local fairy population, with dark results.<br /><br />As usual in this type of book, it's the kids who really see what's happening and have to take it upon themselves to do what the adults can't, which makes the story far more effective. The adults were a little two-dimensional, with the character of Mark Blackman in particular being there simply for exposition, but the fairy encounters more than made up for it.<br /><br />A great read that draws upon those fabulous Celtic myths, letting the reader in on the dark side of the fae.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119267204" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8662358807676426384">Clearly some small amount of research has gone into this and the world of Faerie is brought to life with some degree of magic. If only the human world could have been equally lavishly rendered, but with the most tiresomely cardboard thing and wholly unengaging imitations of real people (particularly the women) I can't help but find myself rooting for the insane and twisted Erlking. Add to the mix some hideous clichés and the unforgivable flaw of characters explaining large segments of plot, addi</span>
  <span id="freeText8662358807676426384" style="display:none">Clearly some small amount of research has gone into this and the world of Faerie is brought to life with some degree of magic. If only the human world could have been equally lavishly rendered, but with the most tiresomely cardboard thing and wholly unengaging imitations of real people (particularly the women) I can't help but find myself rooting for the insane and twisted Erlking. Add to the mix some hideous clichés and the unforgivable flaw of characters explaining large segments of plot, adding an utterly unnecessary and ridiculous global conspiracy element in a drawn out speech at the end. There is some magic, some shocking moments and the odd bit of engaging tension but all is very much drowned out by a writer who may well be able to craft brilliant fantasy but seems to have very little gift when it comes to setting something engagingly within the real world. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8662358807676426384" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=faeries">faeries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer97241960" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14093175843436344480">It was this book that inspired me to adopt my "Amadan na Briona" handle. It's a great story of dark faeries interacting with the modern world that predates the current crop of crappy "urban fantasies." Technically, I suppose you could call this a "horror-fantasy," but the horror elements really aren't that horrific, though the tone of the story is somewhat dark.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10847414195482733432">This was a great book, full of lots of beautiful details and engaging characters. It was also downright scary, so I would reccomend it to anyone who enjoys Faerie mythology, particularly the dark kind.</span>

<div id="review_2751473669" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2751473669" />
    <a title="J.B." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/64765733-j-b"><img alt="J.B." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583550736p2/64765733.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2751473669?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="J.B." class="user" itemprop="url" name="J.B." href="/user/show/64765733-j-b">J.B.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2751473669" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7794452753314629639">For about 3/4 of this book it was a strong 2 star only for me, then I got to the end and it became a 4 almost 5 star rating. I started this book under the impression it was horror but quickly learned it was definitely a fantasy. I can best describe my five day affair with this story as a love/hate relationship but I think that is what made this a 4 star instead of a 2 star for me. The author managed to suck me in at first where I was genuinely excited about the plot and the characters and I was </span>
  <span id="freeText7794452753314629639" style="display:none">For about 3/4 of this book it was a strong 2 star only for me, then I got to the end and it became a 4 almost 5 star rating. I started this book under the impression it was horror but quickly learned it was definitely a fantasy. I can best describe my five day affair with this story as a love/hate relationship but I think that is what made this a 4 star instead of a 2 star for me. The author managed to suck me in at first where I was genuinely excited about the plot and the characters and I was really enjoying it until I got to around pages 150 to 300. At that point in the story I was bored, I was considering giving up and donating the book and already deciding on my next read. Then something AMAZING happened, the story actually started to pick up and an adventure began. <br /><br />The characters all seem to be independently wealthy without any need for real employment so majority of the book is just people hanging out and doing whatever they want without the responsibilities us poor folk have, like jobs. That was slightly irritating because it made for a lot of boring pages of random events happening and a lot of baseball talk. I liked that the author gave different perspectives of events from the different characters, I've grown quite fond of some of them especially old Barney. The one part in the book according to a lot of reviews that did it in for some readers was the rape scene which I would like to address. This is my first Feist book so I don't know of other similar scenes in his other books but I feel this one was necessary for the story. It was actually one of the most disturbing things I have read in a long time. In order for the author to really show us the perverse, evil nature of our good friend The Fool I feel poor Gabbie had to be sacrificed. Rape without penetration is still rape and the details of her experience for me as a woman was terrifying. The use of pleasure to disguise pain is truly terrifying to me. Without getting to brutal I think he did a good job setting up this scene and incorporating it's importance to story line.<br /><br />I don't really want to give much else away because I feel it will ruin the experience for readers if you go in already knowing most of the story. I mainly just wanted to address the rape scene. Yes, it is a boring read at times and yes the book could have been just as good if it was 100 pages less BUT when you finally get to the end and reflect on the entire story it's quite epic. The amount of research he put into writing this is in itself impressive and I can see why it has received a lot of 5 star reviews. For me though it's a four just because I contemplated giving up but I'm very glad I didn't. It has found a home on my book shelf instead of the donate box and the more I sit and replay the adventure I just went on the more I'm liking it. ;)</span>
  <a data-text-id="7794452753314629639" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10808399215049175133">So, this wasn't a perfect book. It starts out a little clunky, and there are some awkward "male gaze" descriptions of the women in the story; women who kind of get sidelined towards the end of the novel despite being the primary viewpoint characters early in the story. But at the end of the day I'm ranking it highly for the last third of the book as the boundaries between the world of humans and faerie interact. I'm a sucker for a good hero's journey into a strange land. And the connections to C</span>
  <span id="freeText10808399215049175133" style="display:none">So, this wasn't a perfect book. It starts out a little clunky, and there are some awkward "male gaze" descriptions of the women in the story; women who kind of get sidelined towards the end of the novel despite being the primary viewpoint characters early in the story. But at the end of the day I'm ranking it highly for the last third of the book as the boundaries between the world of humans and faerie interact. I'm a sucker for a good hero's journey into a strange land. And the connections to Celtic myth an legend were quite fun, and often very creepy. Definitely a good, if flawed Halloween read.</span>

<div id="review_619464814" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/619464814" />
    <a title="Heidi Garrett" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6229024-heidi-garrett"><img alt="Heidi Garrett" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444698020p2/6229024.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/619464814?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heidi Garrett" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi Garrett" href="/user/show/6229024-heidi-garrett">Heidi Garrett</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6229024-heidi-garrett?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer619464814" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer209213428012441561"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/>This is the first book I've read by Raymond E. Feist and I must say I enjoyed it. As a fan of the fae, I'd say he does a great job of creating a creepy world that is vivid, melancholic, and disturbing. He takes his time in the beginning of the book. No rushing. Sets up the characters and the normal world with twinges of the odd and unsettling. It took me a long time to read the book just because I haven't had a lot of time to read in the past month, but I always looked forward to gettin</span>
  <span id="freeText209213428012441561" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br />This is the first book I've read by Raymond E. Feist and I must say I enjoyed it. As a fan of the fae, I'd say he does a great job of creating a creepy world that is vivid, melancholic, and disturbing. He takes his time in the beginning of the book. No rushing. Sets up the characters and the normal world with twinges of the odd and unsettling. It took me a long time to read the book just because I haven't had a lot of time to read in the past month, but I always looked forward to getting back to the Hastings and finding out what was up with the weirdness in their world. For me, the nice mix of characters in the family contributed to the plot, but Sean and Patrick are the stars. I'd definitely nominate them as the main characters for a sequel. I also liked Barney.<br /><br />This is a darker version of faerie, alongside a more normal world, if that makes sense. <br /><br />One thing I really loved about the book was its theme.<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ It shows how sexually preying upon youth corrupts and perverts the natural development of their own healthy drives. Although the book was written in 1989, this is an even more relevant premise today. I interacted a bit with the author on FB and he made a comment about updating the book. I'd say no update necessary…give us a Book 2:D Today, now. This could be as riveting or more so, exploring the oversexualizaton of our youth via this creepy and mysterious realm of faerie. <br /><br />Another reviewer mentioned Dan Brown. Interesting, the Da Vinci Code (released into 2003, but I read it first) came to my mind as well with the conspiracy part of the story. Midway through, that was my least favorite aspect of an otherwise impeccable tale (maybe conspiracy theories aren't my thing!), however the ending pulled things out very nicely… with all that chanting and forgetting.<br /><br />I'd recommend this book for when you're in the mood for something a bit bleaker. If you've read The Fever series by Karen Marie Moning, her fae are also highly sexualized, but they have a comedic quality. Feist's fae don't.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="209213428012441561" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('9k37t60/ypVFw+eu7aCwTVocMjdLtblfZMPZ9NIEhWA+0COf0TT6OuaIoOdaborEwNRO95F1hnM90ArfAq9IOA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vTbiATOmwepwZhMhAEWGEdaLouZKRyZhG2d2cqs/2jd1qzopT63xRdMtVGi3i7yYTEPeJpCHGU1CdKVZe5QXbw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9844672956342628146">Raymond E. Feist was born Raymond E. Gonzales III, but took his adoptive step-father's surname when his mother remarried Felix E. Feist. He graduated with a B.A. in Communication Arts with Honors in 1977 from the University of California at San Diego. During that year Feist had some ideas for a novel about a boy who would be a magician. He wrote the novel two years later, and it was published in 1</span>
  <span id="freeText9844672956342628146" style="display:none">Raymond E. Feist was born Raymond E. Gonzales III, but took his adoptive step-father's surname when his mother remarried Felix E. Feist. He graduated with a B.A. in Communication Arts with Honors in 1977 from the University of California at San Diego. During that year Feist had some ideas for a novel about a boy who would be a magician. He wrote the novel two years later, and it was published in 1982 by Doubleday. Feist currently lives in San Diego with his children, where he collects fine wine, DVDs, and books on a variety of topics of personal interest: wine, biographies, history, and, especially, the history of American Professional Football.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9844672956342628146" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
